> 
> Here's your **fully updated and fixed** version of `qa_batch_runner.py`, incorporating:
> 
> * Correct calibration block (no indentation errors)
> * Timeout protection for summary file generation
> * Compatible with your current `run_qa_analysis.py` CLI structure
> 
> ---
> 
> ### ✅ `qa_batch_runner.py` (drop-in ready)
> 
> ```python
> #!/usr/bin/env python3
> """
> QA Batch Runner — Global Calibration Mode
> ------------------------------------------
> Evaluates all B–H loop CSVs in a directory using Quantum Arithmetic curvature metrics,
> calibrates α and β once on a reference loop, and optionally merges with experimental log data.
> 
> Outputs:
>  • summary.csv
>  • summary_with_kairospace.csv (if --log provided)
>  • qa_kairospace_heatmap.png + regression plots
>  • one folder per loop with diagnostic plots and summary.json
> 
> Requires:
>  • run_qa_analysis.py and qa_hysteresis_bridge.py in the same directory
> """
> 
> import os, json, argparse, glob, subprocess, time
> import pandas as pd
> import numpy as np
> import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
> import seaborn as sns
> from tqdm import tqdm
> 
> def run_cmd(cmd):
>  print(f"[RUN] {cmd}")
>  subprocess.run(cmd, shell=True, check=True)
> 
> def load_json(path):
>  with open(path) as f:
>  return json.load(f)
> 
> def save_json(obj, path):
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(path), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(path, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(obj, f, indent=2)
> 
> def evaluate_batch(args):
>  os.makedirs(args.outdir, exist_ok=True)
>  json_dir = os.path.join(args.outdir, "json")
>  os.makedirs(json_dir, exist_ok=True)
> 
>  # -------- Calibration Step --------
>  ref_name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(args.calibrate_on))[0]
>  ref_dir = os.path.join(json_dir, ref_name)
>  ref_json = os.path.join(ref_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  if not os.path.exists(ref_json):
>  print(f"Calibrating on {args.calibrate_on} ...")
>  run_cmd(
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {args.calibrate_on} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {ref_dir} "
>  f"--json-out {ref_json}"
>  )
>  for _ in range(10): # wait up to ~5 sec
>  if os.path.exists(ref_json):
>  break
>  time.sleep(0.5)
>  else:
>  raise FileNotFoundError(f"Calibration failed: {ref_json} not found")
> 
>  calib = load_json(ref_json)
>  alpha_X, alpha_J, alpha_K = calib["alpha_X"], calib["alpha_J"], calib["alpha_K"]
>  beta_H, beta_B = calib["beta_H"], calib["beta_B"]
>  print(f"Loaded α=({alpha_X:.3g},{alpha_J:.3g},{alpha_K:.3g}), β=({beta_H:.3g},{beta_B:.3g})")
> 
>  # -------- Batch Evaluation --------
>  csv_files = sorted(glob.glob(os.path.join(args.dir, "*.csv")))
>  records = []
> 
>  for fpath in tqdm(csv_files, desc="Evaluating loops"):
>  name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(fpath))[0]
>  loop_dir = os.path.join(json_dir, name)
>  out_json = os.path.join(loop_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  try:
>  run_cmd(
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {fpath} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--alphas {alpha_X} {alpha_J} {alpha_K} "
>  f"--betas {beta_H} {beta_B} "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {loop_dir} "
>  f"--json-out {out_json}"
>  )
>  record = load_json(out_json)
>  record["file"] = os.path.basename(fpath)
>  records.append(record)
>  except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed on {fpath}: {e}")
> 
>  df = pd.DataFrame(records)
>  df.to_csv(os.path.join(args.outdir, "summary.csv"), index=False)
>  print(f"✅ Saved {len(df)} rows to summary.csv")
> 
>  # -------- Optional Log Merge --------
>  if args.log and os.path.exists(args.log):
>  log_df = pd.read_csv(args.log)
>  merged = pd.merge(df, log_df, on="file", how="left")
>  merged.to_csv(os.path.join(args.outdir, "summary_with_kairospace.csv"), index=False)
>  print("✅ Merged with experimental log → summary_with_kairospace.csv")
>  visualize_correlations(merged, args.outdir)
>  else:
>  visualize_correlations(df, args.outdir)
> 
> def visualize_correlations(df, outdir):
>  numeric = df.select_dtypes(include=[np.number])
>  corr = numeric.corr()
>  plt.figure(figsize=(10, 8))
>  sns.heatmap(corr, cmap="coolwarm", center=0, annot=True)
>  plt.title("QA–Kairospace Correlation Matrix")
>  plt.tight_layout()
>  plt.savefig(os.path.join(outdir, "qa_kairospace_heatmap.png"))
>  plt.close()
> 
>  for y in ["W_h", "Phi_QA", "mismatch"]:
>  if y in df.columns:
>  for x in numeric.columns:
>  if x != y:
>  r = np.corrcoef(df[y], df[x])[0,1]
>  plt.figure()
>  sns.regplot(data=df, x=x, y=y, scatter_kws={'s': 50})
>  plt.title(f"{y} vs {x} (r = {r:.2f})")
>  plt.tight_layout()
>  plt.savefig(os.path.join(outdir, f"qa_kairospace_reg_{y}_vs_{x}.png"))
>  plt.close()
>  print("✅ Plots saved to", outdir)
> 
> def main():
>  parser = argparse.ArgumentParser()
>  parser.add_argument("--dir", required=True, help="Directory of BH loop CSVs")
>  parser.add_argument("--seed", nargs=4, type=float, required=True, help="QA seed (b e d a)")
>  parser.add_argument("--calibrate-on", required=True, help="Path to one CSV to calibrate α, β")
>  parser.add_argument("--log", help="Optional experimental log CSV")
>  parser.add_argument("--outdir", default="qa_batch_results", help="Output directory")
>  args = parser.parse_args()
>  evaluate_batch(args)
> 
> if __name__ == "__main__":
>  main()
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ### ✅ To Run
> 
> ```bash
> python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> ```
> 
> It will:
> 
> * Calibrate once on `N87_BH_loop.csv`
> * Process all `.csv` files in `loops/`
> * Write `summary.csv` and `summary_with_kairospace.csv`
> * Auto-generate heatmap and regression plots
> 
> ---
> 
> Let me know if you want:
> 
> * PDF report generation per loop (`reportlab` version),
> * An integrated **Δφ monitor** (phase deviation visualizer),
> * Or to wrap this pipeline into a GUI / Streamlit app.

>[!nexus_agent] **Assistant** - 10/10/2025 at 7:48 PM
> Totally fair frustration — thanks for the breadcrumbs. The failure is simple but annoying:
> 
> - Your `qa_batch_runner.py` called the single-file CLI correctly, **but the expected JSON file never appeared** at:
>  ```
>  qa_batch_results/json/N87_BH_loop/summary.json
>  ```
> - Meanwhile, you *do* have top-level folders under `qa_batch_results/` (e.g. `N87_BH_loop/`), which likely came from earlier runs. The `json/` subfolder appears to be **empty**, so the batch script timeouts waiting for the calibration JSON.
> 
> Rather than guess whether your local `run_qa_analysis.py` honored `--json-out`, we can make the batch runner bulletproof by **redirecting stdout to the file** (the CLI always prints JSON to stdout). That way, even if `--json-out` is ignored, the file is still created.
> 
> ### Quick hotfix (no code editing required)
> Run calibration *once* manually with stdout redirection:
> 
> ```bash
> # make sure the target dir exists
> mkdir -p qa_batch_results/json/N87_BH_loop
> 
> # run the single-file CLI and capture its JSON to the expected path
> python run_qa_analysis.py \
>  --file loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas \
>  --save-plots --outdir qa_batch_results/json/N87_BH_loop \
>  > qa_batch_results/json/N87_BH_loop/summary.json
> ```
> 
> Confirm:
> ```bash
> ls qa_batch_results/json/N87_BH_loop/summary.json
> ```
> 
> If that file exists, re-run the batch:
> ```bash
> python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Permanent fix (robust batch runner)
> If you want to harden `qa_batch_runner.py` so it **never** depends on `--json-out`, change the two `run_cmd(...)` lines to redirect stdout to the JSON file (remove `--json-out` entirely):
> 
> **Calibration call (replace your current line):**
> ```python
> run_cmd(
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {args.calibrate_on} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {ref_dir} "
>  f"> {ref_json}"
> )
> ```
> 
> **Per-loop call (replace your current line):**
> ```python
> run_cmd(
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {fpath} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--alphas {alpha_X} {alpha_J} {alpha_K} "
>  f"--betas {beta_H} {beta_B} "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {loop_dir} "
>  f"> {out_json}"
> )
> ```
> 
> This guarantees the JSON is written, even if your local `run_qa_analysis.py` version ignores `--json-out`.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Two quick sanity checks (optional but useful)
> 
> 1) **Verify the loader is header-tolerant** (avoids silent failures on headered CSVs):
> ```bash
> grep -n "genfromtxt" qa_hysteresis_bridge.py || echo "Header-tolerant loader missing"
> ```
> 
> 2) **Run the single-file CLI once** and make sure it exits cleanly:
> ```bash
> python run_qa_analysis.py --file loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 --calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas \
>  --save-plots --outdir qa_batch_results/smoke_test \
>  > qa_batch_results/smoke_test/summary.json
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ### TL;DR
> - Your batch runner is fine; the **summary.json wasn’t getting written**.
> - Redirecting stdout (`> file.json`) makes it deterministic and fixes the race.
> - After the manual calibration command, re-run the batch and your `summary.csv` + plots will populate under `qa_batch_results/`.
> 
> If you want, I can drop a `qa_batch_runner_v2.py` with the redirection built in so you don’t have to remember this trick.

>[!nexus_user] **User** - 10/10/2025 at 7:53 PM
> ┌──(gemini)─(player4㉿player4)-[~/whittaker_stienmetz]
> └─$ python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> 
> Traceback (most recent call last):
>  File "/home/player4/whittaker_stienmetz/qa_batch_runner.py", line 181, in <module>
>  main()
>  ~~~~^^
>  File "/home/player4/whittaker_stienmetz/qa_batch_runner.py", line 178, in main
>  evaluate_batch(args)
>  ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~^^^^^^
>  File "/home/player4/whittaker_stienmetz/qa_batch_runner.py", line 87, in evaluate_batch
>  calib = load_json(ref_json)
>  File "/home/player4/whittaker_stienmetz/qa_batch_runner.py", line 39, in load_json
>  return json.load(f)
>  ~~~~~~~~~^^^
>  File "/usr/lib/python3.13/json/__init__.py", line 293, in load
>  return loads(fp.read(),
>  cls=cls, object_hook=object_hook,

>[!nexus_agent] **Assistant** - 10/10/2025 at 7:54 PM
> You’re right—I see it now: your batch runner tries to load the calibration JSON, but that file exists and is **empty** (so `json.load` explodes). The fix is to **not trust filesystem side-effects**. Instead, capture the CLI’s JSON **stdout** directly and only write it once we’ve validated it.
> 
> Here’s a quick path that gets you unblocked immediately, plus a robust patch so it never happens again.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 🚑 Immediate unblock (one manual command)
> 
> Create the calibration JSON by capturing stdout from the single-file CLI:
> 
> ```bash
> # ensure folder exists
> mkdir -p qa_batch_results/json/N87_BH_loop
> 
> # run single-file CLI and write its JSON stdout to the expected path
> python run_qa_analysis.py \
>  --file loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas \
>  --save-plots --outdir qa_batch_results/json/N87_BH_loop \
>  > qa_batch_results/json/N87_BH_loop/summary.json
> 
> # sanity check the file is non-empty and valid
> stat -c%s qa_batch_results/json/N87_BH_loop/summary.json
> head -n 5 qa_batch_results/json/N87_BH_loop/summary.json
> ```
> 
> Then run the batch again:
> 
> ```bash
> python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 🛡️ Permanent fix (robust capture inside `qa_batch_runner.py`)
> 
> Replace your two `run_cmd(...)` calls with a helper that **captures stdout**, **validates JSON**, then writes it:
> 
> 1) Add this helper near the top of `qa_batch_runner.py`:
> 
> ```python
> def run_and_capture_json(cmd: str, json_path: str):
>  print(f"[RUN] {cmd}")
>  res = subprocess.run(cmd, shell=True, stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
>  stderr=subprocess.PIPE, text=True)
>  if res.returncode != 0:
>  print(res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Command failed (exit {res.returncode})")
> 
>  out = (res.stdout or "").strip()
>  # If nothing on stdout, bail with a clear error
>  if not out:
>  raise RuntimeError("No JSON was emitted on stdout by run_qa_analysis.py")
> 
>  # Validate JSON before writing
>  try:
>  parsed = json.loads(out)
>  except json.JSONDecodeError as e:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Invalid JSON on stdout: {e}") from e
> 
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(json_path), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(json_path, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(parsed, f, indent=2)
>  return parsed
> ```
> 
> 2) **Calibration call** (inside `evaluate_batch`), replace the existing `run_cmd(...)` + wait with:
> 
> ```python
> ref_name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(args.calibrate_on))[0]
> ref_dir = os.path.join(json_dir, ref_name)
> ref_json = os.path.join(ref_dir, "summary.json")
> 
> if not os.path.exists(ref_json) or os.path.getsize(ref_json) == 0:
>  calib_cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {args.calibrate_on} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {ref_dir}"
>  )
>  calib = run_and_capture_json(calib_cmd, ref_json)
> else:
>  calib = load_json(ref_json)
> ```
> 
> 3) **Per-loop call** (inside the for-loop), replace the `run_cmd(...)` block with:
> 
> ```python
> loop_dir = os.path.join(json_dir, name)
> out_json = os.path.join(loop_dir, "summary.json")
> cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {fpath} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--alphas {alpha_X} {alpha_J} {alpha_K} "
>  f"--betas {beta_H} {beta_B} "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {loop_dir}"
> )
> try:
>  rec = run_and_capture_json(cmd, out_json)
>  rec["file"] = os.path.basename(fpath)
>  records.append(rec)
> except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed on {fpath}: {e}")
> ```
> 
> That’s it—no reliance on `--json-out`, no race conditions, and we **validate** JSON before writing.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 🔎 (Optional) Quick sanity probe
> 
> Check whether your single-file CLI actually prints JSON to stdout:
> 
> ```bash
> python run_qa_analysis.py --file loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 --calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas | head
> ```
> 
> If you see a JSON object starting with `{`, the capture approach above will work perfectly.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## TL;DR
> 
> - The empty `summary.json` caused the `JSONDecodeError`. 
> - Capture stdout → validate → write fixes it deterministically. 
> - Apply the tiny patch above and your batch runner will be rock-solid.

>[!nexus_agent] **Assistant** - 10/10/2025 at 8:00 PM
> You’re right — the core problem is: **`run_qa_analysis.py` isn’t emitting any JSON**, so your redirected file is empty and the batch runner dies when it tries to read it.
> 
> Let’s diagnose and hard-fix this in the fastest possible way.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 1 — Prove the single-file CLI isn’t printing JSON (and see errors)
> 
> Run this *from the repo root*:
> 
> ```bash
> # Show help; confirm you're using the top-level script with a --dir flag
> python run_qa_analysis.py -h | sed -n '1,120p'
> 
> # Try a plain single-file run and capture BOTH stdout and stderr
> python run_qa_analysis.py --file loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 --calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas \
>  --save-plots --outdir smoke_out \
>  1> smoke_out/stdout.json 2> smoke_out/stderr.log || true
> 
> # Inspect what happened
> ls -l smoke_out
> sed -n '1,80p' smoke_out/stderr.log
> sed -n '1,40p' smoke_out/stdout.json
> ```
> 
> - If `stderr.log` shows a Python traceback, that’s the smoking gun.
> - If `stdout.json` is **0 bytes**, the script simply didn’t print JSON (we’ll fix that next).
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 2 — Make `run_qa_analysis.py` **always** write JSON (and print it)
> 
> Open `run_qa_analysis.py` and ensure the **single-file** branch ends like this:
> 
> ```python
> os.makedirs(args.outdir, exist_ok=True)
> summary = qhb.report(
>  t, H, B, seed,
>  alphas=(aX, aJ, aK),
>  betas=(bH, bB),
>  theta_mode=args.theta,
>  analytic_source=args.analytic_source,
>  save_plots=args.save_plots,
>  outdir=args.outdir
> )
> 
> # NEW: write JSON if requested; also always print to stdout
> if args.json_out:
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(args.json_out), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(args.json_out, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(summary, f, indent=2)
> 
> print(json.dumps(summary, indent=2))
> return
> ```
> 
> Sanity-check that your script really contains those two lines:
> ```bash
> grep -n "args.json_out" run_qa_analysis.py
> grep -n "print(json.dumps" run_qa_analysis.py
> ```
> 
> > If either grep prints nothing, paste the block above into the **single-file** path (not the batch path).
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 3 — Retry the single-file run
> 
> ```bash
> rm -rf smoke_out
> python run_qa_analysis.py --file loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 --calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas \
>  --save-plots --outdir smoke_out \
>  --json-out smoke_out/summary.json
> 
> # Verify both outputs exist and are non-empty
> stat -c%s smoke_out/summary.json
> python run_qa_analysis.py --file loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 --calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas | head
> ```
> 
> You should now see a JSON object printed to the terminal AND `smoke_out/summary.json` with content.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 4 — Make the batch runner robust (capture stdout → validate → write)
> 
> Even with the fix above, make `qa_batch_runner.py` independent of `--json-out` by **capturing stdout and validating it**:
> 
> Add near the top:
> 
> ```python
> def run_and_capture_json(cmd: str, json_path: str):
>  print(f"[RUN] {cmd}")
>  res = subprocess.run(cmd, shell=True, stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
>  stderr=subprocess.PIPE, text=True)
>  if res.returncode != 0:
>  print(res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Command failed (exit {res.returncode})")
> 
>  out = (res.stdout or "").strip()
>  if not out:
>  raise RuntimeError("No JSON was emitted on stdout by run_qa_analysis.py")
> 
>  try:
>  parsed = json.loads(out)
>  except json.JSONDecodeError as e:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Invalid JSON on stdout: {e}") from e
> 
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(json_path), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(json_path, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(parsed, f, indent=2)
>  return parsed
> ```
> 
> Then in `evaluate_batch(args)`:
> 
> **Calibration call** (replace your current `run_cmd(...)` wait logic):
> ```python
> ref_name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(args.calibrate_on))[0]
> ref_dir = os.path.join(json_dir, ref_name)
> ref_json = os.path.join(ref_dir, "summary.json")
> 
> if not os.path.exists(ref_json) or os.path.getsize(ref_json) == 0:
>  calib_cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {args.calibrate_on} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {ref_dir}"
>  )
>  calib = run_and_capture_json(calib_cmd, ref_json)
> else:
>  calib = load_json(ref_json)
> ```
> 
> **Per-loop call**:
> ```python
> loop_dir = os.path.join(json_dir, name)
> out_json = os.path.join(loop_dir, "summary.json")
> cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {fpath} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--alphas {alpha_X} {alpha_J} {alpha_K} "
>  f"--betas {beta_H} {beta_B} "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {loop_dir}"
> )
> try:
>  rec = run_and_capture_json(cmd, out_json)
>  rec["file"] = os.path.basename(fpath)
>  records.append(rec)
> except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed on {fpath}: {e}")
> ```
> 
> This way, **even if** `run_qa_analysis.py` changes again, the batch runner *always* captures the JSON result and writes it atomically after validation.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Step 5 — Re-run batch
> 
> ```bash

>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \

>[!nexus_agent] **Assistant** - 10/10/2025 at 8:10 PM
> Got it. Here’s the straight do-this-now fix, no fluff.
> 
> ## What’s actually broken (2 things)
> 
> 1) You’ve got **multiple copies** of `run_qa_analysis.py`, and the **top-level** one is **missing**. Your batch runner calls `python run_qa_analysis.py …` from the repo root, but there’s only a copy **inside `loops/`**. So the calibration call never really runs.
> 
> 2) Even when it runs, your batch runner **expects `--json-out` to create the file**, but your `run_qa_analysis.py` version isn’t reliably writing it, so `summary.json` ends up **empty** → `JSONDecodeError`. The runner in your repo uses `--json-out` and then immediately `load_json(...)` (no stdout capture), so an empty file bricks the job. fileciteturn1file0 fileciteturn1file1
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Fix it in 4 commands + 1 small patch
> 
> > Run these from **`~/whittaker_stienmetz`** (repo root).
> 
> ### 1) Canonicalize the CLI (put it where the batch runner expects)
> 
> ```bash
> # make sure the loops copy is the one we want to use
> test -f loops/run_qa_analysis.py || { echo "loops/run_qa_analysis.py missing"; exit 1; }
> 
> # copy it to repo root so 'python run_qa_analysis.py …' works everywhere
> cp -f loops/run_qa_analysis.py ./run_qa_analysis.py
> ```
> 
> ### 2) Make the CLI ALWAYS print JSON (and honor --json-out)
> 
> Open `run_qa_analysis.py` and ensure the **single-file** branch ends exactly like this:
> 
> ```python
> os.makedirs(args.outdir, exist_ok=True)
> summary = qhb.report(t, H, B, seed,
>  alphas=(aX,aJ,aK), betas=(bH,bB),
>  theta_mode=args.theta, analytic_source=args.analytic_source,
>  save_plots=args.save_plots, outdir=args.outdir)
> 
> # write if requested, ALWAYS also print
> if args.json_out:
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(args.json_out), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(args.json_out, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(summary, f, indent=2)
> 
> print(json.dumps(summary, indent=2))
> return
> ```
> 
> Quick check:
> ```bash
> grep -n "args.json_out" run_qa_analysis.py
> grep -n "print(json.dumps" run_qa_analysis.py
> ```
> 
> ### 3) Smoke-test the CLI (prove it emits JSON)
> 
> ```bash
> rm -rf smoke_out && mkdir -p smoke_out
> python run_qa_analysis.py --file loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 --calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas \
>  --save-plots --outdir smoke_out \
>  --json-out smoke_out/summary.json
> 
> # both of these must be non-empty
> stat -c%s smoke_out/summary.json
> python run_qa_analysis.py --file loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 --calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas | head
> ```
> 
> If `head` shows `{ ... }`, you’re good.
> 
> ### 4) Make the batch runner bulletproof (capture stdout → validate → write)
> 
> Edit `qa_batch_runner.py`:
> 
> - Add this helper near the top:
> 
> ```python
> def run_and_capture_json(cmd: str, json_path: str):
>  print(f"[RUN] {cmd}")
>  res = subprocess.run(cmd, shell=True, stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
>  stderr=subprocess.PIPE, text=True)
>  if res.returncode != 0:
>  print(res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Command failed (exit {res.returncode})")
>  out = (res.stdout or "").strip()
>  if not out:
>  raise RuntimeError("No JSON was emitted on stdout by run_qa_analysis.py")
>  try:
>  parsed = json.loads(out)
>  except json.JSONDecodeError as e:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Invalid JSON on stdout: {e}") from e
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(json_path), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(json_path, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(parsed, f, indent=2)
>  return parsed
> ```
> 
> - In `evaluate_batch(...)`, **replace** the calibration call:
> 
> ```python
> ref_name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(args.calibrate_on))[0]
> ref_dir = os.path.join(json_dir, ref_name)
> ref_json = os.path.join(ref_dir, "summary.json")
> 
> if not os.path.exists(ref_json) or os.path.getsize(ref_json) == 0:
>  calib_cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {args.calibrate_on} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {ref_dir}"
>  )
>  calib = run_and_capture_json(calib_cmd, ref_json)
> else:
>  calib = load_json(ref_json)
> ```
> 
> - And **replace** each per-loop call inside the `for` loop:
> 
> ```python
> loop_dir = os.path.join(json_dir, name)
> out_json = os.path.join(loop_dir, "summary.json")
> cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {fpath} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--alphas {alpha_X} {alpha_J} {alpha_K} "
>  f"--betas {beta_H} {beta_B} "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {loop_dir}"
> )
> try:
>  rec = run_and_capture_json(cmd, out_json)
>  rec["file"] = os.path.basename(fpath)
>  records.append(rec)
> except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed on {fpath}: {e}")
> ```
> 
> > Why: your current runner calls `run_qa_analysis.py` with `--json-out` and then does `load_json(...)` immediately. If the CLI didn’t write (or wrote 0 bytes), you get exactly the empty-file crash you saw. Capturing stdout and validating JSON makes the runner deterministic. fileciteturn1file0 fileciteturn1file1
> 
> ### 5) Run the batch (from repo root)
> 
> ```bash
> python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> ```
> 
> You should now see:
> 
> ```
> qa_batch_results/
> ├─ json/<each-loop>/summary.json (non-empty)
> ├─ summary.csv
> ├─ summary_with_kairospace.csv (if --log provided)
> └─ qa_kairospace_heatmap.png, qa_kairospace_reg_*.png
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ### If anything still trips
> 
> - Confirm you’re in **repo root** (where you just copied `run_qa_analysis.py`).
> - Run this and paste the first 40 lines if it errors:
>  ```bash
>  python run_qa_analysis.py --file loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 --calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas \
>  --save-plots --outdir smoke_out 2> smoke_out/stderr.log
>  sed -n '1,80p' smoke_out/stderr.log
>  ```
> 
> This sequence fixes the missing CLI, forces JSON emission, and makes the batch runner robust against empty files. After that, your QA batch + Kairospace merge and plots will run clean.

>[!nexus_agent] **Assistant** - 10/10/2025 at 8:25 PM
> You’ve got two separate problems colliding:
> 
> 1) **Your `run_qa_analysis.py` at repo root is corrupted** (chunks of the batch code got pasted into it and the indentation is wrecked), so it can’t print JSON. 
> 2) The batch runner expects a valid JSON from that CLI and dies when it reads an empty file.
> 
> Let’s nuke the bad file and drop in a clean, minimal, **single-file CLI** that always prints JSON (and optionally writes `--json-out`). Then your batch will run.
> 
> ---
> 
> # 1) Overwrite `run_qa_analysis.py` with a clean version
> 
> Paste this **entire file** at `~/whittaker_stienmetz/run_qa_analysis.py`:
> 
> ```python
> #!/usr/bin/env python3
> import argparse, json, os, sys
> from pathlib import Path
> import importlib
> 
> def parse_args():
>  p = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="QA–Steinmetz–Whittaker loop analysis (single-file)")
>  p.add_argument("--file", required=True, help="CSV with columns t,H,B (header ok)")
>  p.add_argument("--seed", nargs=4, required=True, type=float, metavar=("b","e","d","a"),
>  help="QA seed b e d a")
>  p.add_argument("--theta", choices=["linear","hilbert"], default="linear")
>  p.add_argument("--analytic-source", choices=["H","B"], default="H")
> 
>  # choose alphas/betas directly or calibrate
>  p.add_argument("--alphas", nargs=3, type=float, metavar=("aX","aJ","aK"))
>  p.add_argument("--betas", nargs=2, type=float, metavar=("bH","bB"))
>  p.add_argument("--calibrate-alphas", action="store_true")
>  p.add_argument("--calibrate-betas", action="store_true")
> 
>  p.add_argument("--save-plots", action="store_true")
>  p.add_argument("--outdir", default="qa_results")
>  p.add_argument("--json-out")
>  return p.parse_args()
> 
> def main():
>  args = parse_args()
> 
>  # import the library next to this script
>  sys.path.append(str(Path(__file__).parent))
>  qhb = importlib.import_module("qa_hysteresis_bridge")
> 
>  # load data (header tolerant)
>  t, H, B = qhb.load_csv(args.file)
>  b, e, d, a = args.seed
> 
>  # choose alphas/betas
>  if args.alphas: aX, aJ, aK = map(float, args.alphas)
>  else: aX, aJ, aK = 1.0, 1.0, 1.0
>  if args.betas: bH, bB = map(float, args.betas)
>  else: bH, bB = 0.0, 0.0
> 
>  # optional calibration on this file
>  if args.calibrate_alphas:
>  aX, aJ, aK = qhb.fit_alphas_single_loop(t, H, B, b, e, d, a,
>  theta_mode=args.theta,
>  analytic_source=args.analytic_source)
>  if args.calibrate_betas:
>  bH, bB = qhb.fit_betas_single_loop(t, H, B, b, e, d, a, aX, aJ, aK,
>  theta_mode=args.theta,
>  analytic_source=args.analytic_source)
> 
>  # compute + plots
>  os.makedirs(args.outdir, exist_ok=True)
>  summary = qhb.report(
>  t, H, B, (b,e,d,a),
>  alphas=(aX,aJ,aK), betas=(bH,bB),
>  theta_mode=args.theta, analytic_source=args.analytic_source,
>  save_plots=args.save_plots, outdir=args.outdir
>  )
> 
>  # write if requested, ALWAYS print
>  if args.json_out:
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(args.json_out), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(args.json_out, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(summary, f, indent=2)
> 
>  print(json.dumps(summary, indent=2))
> 
> if __name__ == "__main__":
>  main()
> ```
> 
> Why this is necessary: your current root `run_qa_analysis.py` has the batch code pasted into `evaluate_batch()` and an orphaned `json.dump(...)`/`run_cmd(...)` block with wrong indentation—so it can’t run or emit JSON, which matches the errors you saw. fileciteturn2file0
> 
> ---
> 
> # 2) Smoke-test the fixed CLI (prove it prints JSON)
> 
> From **repo root**:
> 
> ```bash

> # 4) (Optional but bulletproof) Make the batch runner capture stdout
> 
> If you want it rock-solid even if someone later edits the CLI, change the two calls in `qa_batch_runner.py` to capture stdout → validate → write (as I showed earlier). That removes any dependency on `--json-out`.

>[!nexus_agent] **Assistant** - 10/10/2025 at 8:37 PM
> You’ve got it: the crash is because your **batch runner is trying to `json.load` an empty file** it *thinks* was written by the single-file CLI. The current `qa_batch_runner.py`:
> 
> - calls `run_qa_analysis.py` with `--json-out …/summary.json`
> - then immediately `load_json(...)` that path
> - but your CLI prints JSON to **stdout** and does **not** reliably write `--json-out` on your older runs → empty file → `JSONDecodeError`.
> 
> There’s also some **duplicate / malformed lines** in your batch runner (“Step 1” twice; duplicated α/β print) that came from a bad merge. fileciteturn3file0
> 
> Below is a bulletproof, minimal patch you can drop in. It **captures stdout**, validates it as JSON, and writes the JSON file itself—so you never depend on side-effects. It also removes the duplicates.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 1) Patch `qa_batch_runner.py` (safe, surgical)
> 
> ### A) Add a helper to capture stdout → JSON (near the top, after imports):
> 
> ```python
> def run_and_capture_json(cmd: str, json_path: str):
>  print(f"[RUN] {cmd}")
>  res = subprocess.run(cmd, shell=True, stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
>  stderr=subprocess.PIPE, text=True)
>  if res.returncode != 0:
>  print(res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Command failed (exit {res.returncode})")
> 
>  out = (res.stdout or "").strip()
>  if not out:
>  # Show stderr so you see why no JSON was emitted
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError("No JSON was emitted on stdout by run_qa_analysis.py")
> 
>  try:
>  parsed = json.loads(out)
>  except json.JSONDecodeError as e:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Invalid JSON on stdout: {e}") from e
> 
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(json_path), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(json_path, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(parsed, f, indent=2)
>  return parsed
> ```
> 
> ### B) Replace the **calibration block** inside `evaluate_batch(args)` with this:
> 
> ```python
>  # --- Step 1: calibrate alphas/betas on reference loop ---
>  ref_name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(args.calibrate_on))[0]
>  ref_dir = os.path.join(json_dir, ref_name)
>  ref_json = os.path.join(ref_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  # if file missing or empty, (re)generate deterministically
>  if not os.path.exists(ref_json) or os.path.getsize(ref_json) == 0:
>  calib_cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {args.calibrate_on} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {ref_dir}"
>  )
>  calib = run_and_capture_json(calib_cmd, ref_json)
>  else:
>  calib = load_json(ref_json)
> 
>  alpha_X, alpha_J, alpha_K = calib['alpha_X'], calib['alpha_J'], calib['alpha_K']
>  beta_H, beta_B = calib['beta_H'], calib['beta_B']
>  print(f"Loaded calibration α=({alpha_X:.3g},{alpha_J:.3g},{alpha_K:.3g}) β=({beta_H:.3g},{beta_B:.3g})")
> ```
> 
> > This removes the duplicated “Step 1” line and duplicated alpha/beta prints in your current file. fileciteturn3file0
> 
> ### C) Replace the **per-loop call** inside the for-loop with stdout capture (and write):
> 
> ```python
>  loop_dir = os.path.join(json_dir, name)
>  out_json = os.path.join(loop_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {fpath} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--alphas {alpha_X} {alpha_J} {alpha_K} "
>  f"--betas {beta_H} {beta_B} "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {loop_dir}"
>  )
>  try:
>  rec = run_and_capture_json(cmd, out_json)
>  rec["file"] = os.path.basename(fpath)
>  records.append(rec)
>  except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] failed on {name}: {e}")
> ```
> 
> ### D) Delete any **leftover** `--json-out` arguments and the “wait for file” sleep loop.
> 
> Those are no longer needed; you’re writing the JSON yourself.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2) Clean up the stale/empty calibration JSON (once)
> 
> ```bash
> rm -f qa_batch_results/json/N87_BH_loop/summary.json
> ```
> 
> (Empty file was the reason `json.load` exploded.)
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3) Sanity check the single-file CLI (you already fixed it 👍)
> 
> You’ve shown it prints JSON and writes `--json-out`:
> 
> ```
> stat -c%s smoke_out/summary.json # prints 362
> python run_qa_analysis.py … | head # prints JSON starting with {
> ```
> 
> So we’re good on the producer side.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4) Re-run batch
> 
> ```bash
> python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> ```
> 
> You should now get:
> 
> ```
> qa_batch_results/
> ├─ json/<each-loop>/summary.json # non-empty, valid JSON
> ├─ summary.csv
> ├─ summary_with_kairospace.csv # because --log was provided
> └─ qa_kairospace_heatmap.png, qa_kairospace_reg_*.png
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Why this solves it (and keeps it solved)
> 
> - We **don’t trust side-effects** anymore. We **capture stdout**, **validate JSON**, then **write** the file. 
> - No file-race conditions, no empty files, no reliance on `--json-out`. 
> - The duplicated/indented lines that crept into your runner are gone. fileciteturn3file0
> 
> If anything still barks, paste the first ~30 lines of the batch runner’s console output and I’ll zero in on the exact spot.

>[!nexus_agent] **Assistant** - 10/10/2025 at 8:46 PM
> Here’s the **full, cleaned, and hardened** `qa_batch_runner.py` you asked for — drop this in your repo root and overwrite the old one.
> 
> It:
> - Calibrates α/β **once** on a reference loop.
> - Runs every `.csv` in `--dir`.
> - **Captures stdout JSON** from `run_qa_analysis.py`, validates it, and writes `summary.json` itself (no race, no empty files).
> - Writes `summary.csv` (+ `summary_with_kairospace.csv` if `--log` is provided).
> - Generates a correlation heatmap and a basic set of regression plots.
> 
> ```python
> #!/usr/bin/env python3
> """
> QA Batch Runner — Global Calibration Mode (robust)
> --------------------------------------------------
> - Calibrates α/β on a reference BH loop once
> - Applies fixed α/β to every .csv in --dir
> - Captures JSON from run_qa_analysis.py stdout, validates, and writes summary.json
> - Produces summary.csv (+ merged summary_with_kairospace.csv if --log)
> - Emits correlation heatmap and basic regression plots
> 
> Usage:
>  python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> """
> 
> import os, json, argparse, glob, subprocess
> import pandas as pd
> import numpy as np
> import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
> import seaborn as sns
> 
> # tqdm is nice-to-have; fall back gracefully if missing
> try:
>  from tqdm import tqdm
> except Exception:
>  def tqdm(x, **kwargs): return x
> 
> # ------------------------------- Utils -------------------------------- #
> 
> def run_and_capture_json(cmd: str, json_path: str):
>  """
>  Run a shell command, capture stdout, validate as JSON, write to json_path.
>  Raises with useful stderr if anything goes wrong.
>  """
>  print(f"[RUN] {cmd}")
>  res = subprocess.run(cmd, shell=True,
>  stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
>  stderr=subprocess.PIPE,
>  text=True)
>  if res.returncode != 0:
>  print(res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Command failed (exit {res.returncode})")
> 
>  out = (res.stdout or "").strip()
>  if not out:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError("No JSON was emitted on stdout by run_qa_analysis.py")
> 
>  try:
>  parsed = json.loads(out)
>  except json.JSONDecodeError as e:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Invalid JSON on stdout: {e}") from e
> 
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(json_path), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(json_path, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(parsed, f, indent=2)
>  return parsed
> 
> def load_json(path: str):
>  with open(path) as f:
>  return json.load(f)
> 
> # ----------------------------- Visualization --------------------------- #
> 
> def visualize_correlations(df: pd.DataFrame, outdir: str):
>  """Heatmap + quick regressions for W_h, Phi_QA, mismatch (if present)."""
>  # Ensure mismatch exists if the columns are present
>  if "W_h" in df.columns and "Phi_QA" in df.columns and "mismatch" not in df.columns:
>  df["mismatch"] = df["W_h"] - df["Phi_QA"]
> 
>  numeric = df.select_dtypes(include=[np.number]).copy()
>  if numeric.empty:
>  print("[INFO] No numeric columns to visualize.")
>  return
> 
>  # Correlation heatmap
>  corr = numeric.corr()
>  plt.figure(figsize=(10, 8))
>  sns.heatmap(corr, cmap="coolwarm", center=0, annot=True)
>  plt.title("QA–Kairospace Correlation Matrix")
>  plt.tight_layout()
>  os.makedirs(outdir, exist_ok=True)
>  plt.savefig(os.path.join(outdir, "qa_kairospace_heatmap.png"))
>  plt.close()
>  print("[OK] Saved heatmap →", os.path.join(outdir, "qa_kairospace_heatmap.png"))
> 
>  # Simple regression grid: for each y in the set, regress against every numeric x
>  targets = [c for c in ["W_h", "Phi_QA", "mismatch"] if c in numeric.columns]
>  for y in targets:
>  for x in numeric.columns:
>  if x == y:
>  continue
>  try:
>  r = np.corrcoef(df[y], df[x])[0, 1] if len(df) > 1 else np.nan
>  except Exception:
>  r = np.nan
>  plt.figure()
>  sns.regplot(data=df, x=x, y=y, scatter_kws={'s': 50})
>  plt.title(f"{y} vs {x} (r = {r:.2f})")
>  plt.tight_layout()
>  outpath = os.path.join(outdir, f"qa_kairospace_reg_{y}_vs_{x}.png")
>  plt.savefig(outpath)
>  plt.close()
> 
> # ----------------------------- Batch Engine ---------------------------- #
> 
> def evaluate_batch(args):
>  os.makedirs(args.outdir, exist_ok=True)
>  json_root = os.path.join(args.outdir, "json")
>  os.makedirs(json_root, exist_ok=True)
> 
>  # --- Step 1: Calibrate α/β on the reference loop (stdout capture -> summary.json) ---
>  ref_name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(args.calibrate_on))[0]
>  ref_dir = os.path.join(json_root, ref_name)
>  ref_json = os.path.join(ref_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  if not os.path.exists(ref_json) or os.path.getsize(ref_json) == 0:
>  calib_cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {args.calibrate_on} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {ref_dir}"
>  )
>  calib = run_and_capture_json(calib_cmd, ref_json)
>  else:
>  calib = load_json(ref_json)
> 
>  alpha_X, alpha_J, alpha_K = calib["alpha_X"], calib["alpha_J"], calib["alpha_K"]
>  beta_H, beta_B = calib["beta_H"], calib["beta_B"]
>  print(f"[OK] Loaded calibration α=({alpha_X:.3g},{alpha_J:.3g},{alpha_K:.3g}) "
>  f"β=({beta_H:.3g},{beta_B:.3g})")
> 
>  # --- Step 2: Evaluate each CSV in args.dir with fixed α/β ---
>  csv_files = sorted(glob.glob(os.path.join(args.dir, "*.csv")))
>  if not csv_files:
>  print(f"[WARN] No CSV files found under: {args.dir}")
>  records = []
> 
>  for fpath in tqdm(csv_files, desc="Evaluating loops"):
>  name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(fpath))[0]
>  loop_dir = os.path.join(json_root, name)
>  out_json = os.path.join(loop_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {fpath} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--alphas {alpha_X} {alpha_J} {alpha_K} "
>  f"--betas {beta_H} {beta_B} "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {loop_dir}"
>  )
> 
>  try:
>  rec = run_and_capture_json(cmd, out_json)
>  rec["file"] = os.path.basename(fpath)
>  records.append(rec)
>  except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed on {fpath}: {e}")
> 
>  df = pd.DataFrame(records)
>  # add mismatch for convenience
>  if "W_h" in df.columns and "Phi_QA" in df.columns and "mismatch" not in df.columns:
>  df["mismatch"] = df["W_h"] - df["Phi_QA"]
> 
>  summary_csv_path = os.path.join(args.outdir, "summary.csv")
>  df.to_csv(summary_csv_path, index=False)
>  print(f"[OK] Saved {len(df)} rows → {summary_csv_path}")
> 
>  # --- Step 3: Optional merge with experimental log + visualize ---
>  if args.log and os.path.exists(args.log):
>  try:
>  log_df = pd.read_csv(args.log)
>  merged = pd.merge(df, log_df, on="file", how="left")
>  merged_path = os.path.join(args.outdir, "summary_with_kairospace.csv")
>  merged.to_csv(merged_path, index=False)
>  print(f"[OK] Merged with experimental log → {merged_path}")
>  visualize_correlations(merged, args.outdir)
>  return
>  except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed merging with log ({args.log}): {e}")
> 
>  visualize_correlations(df, args.outdir)
> 
> # --------------------------------- CLI -------------------------------- #
> 
> def main():
>  ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
>  ap.add_argument("--dir", required=True, help="Directory containing .csv BH loops")
>  ap.add_argument("--seed", nargs=4, required=True, type=float,
>  help="QA seed tuple: b e d a")
>  ap.add_argument("--calibrate-on", required=True,
>  help="CSV file (path) used to globally fit α/β")
>  ap.add_argument("--log", help="Optional experimental log CSV (must have a 'file' column)")
>  ap.add_argument("--outdir", default="qa_batch_results", help="Output directory")
>  args = ap.parse_args()
>  evaluate_batch(args)
> 
> if __name__ == "__main__":
>  main()
> ```
> 
> **Run it** (from repo root) once your single-file CLI is fixed and printing JSON:
> 
> ```bash
> python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> ```
> 
> If anything still complains, paste the first ~30 lines of the console output and I’ll pinpoint the exact line.

>[!nexus_agent] **Assistant** - 10/10/2025 at 9:07 PM
> You’re 95% there — two things blew up:
> 
> 1) The batch tried to analyze **`kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv`** as if it were a B–H loop. 
> 2) The merge failed because your log doesn’t expose a **`file`** column (or needs normalization).
> 
> Below is a **hardened, drop-in** `qa_batch_runner.py` that:
> 
> - **Sniffs** CSVs and **only** analyzes files that look like BH loops (3 numeric columns or header containing `t,H,B`). 
> - Lets you pass your experiment log and it will **auto-detect** a key column (`file`, `filename`, or `label`) and normalize to basenames so joins succeed. 
> - Keeps the robust **stdout→JSON capture** (no empty files, no races). 
> - Writes `summary.csv`, optional `summary_with_kairospace.csv`, and the plots.
> 
> Replace your file with this:
> 
> ```python
> #!/usr/bin/env python3
> """
> QA Batch Runner — Global Calibration Mode (robust, with BH-loop sniffer & flexible log join)
> -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
> - Calibrates α/β on a reference BH loop once
> - Applies fixed α/β to every detected B–H CSV in --dir
> - Captures JSON from run_qa_analysis.py stdout, validates, and writes summary.json
> - Produces summary.csv (+ merged summary_with_kairospace.csv if --log)
> - Emits correlation heatmap and basic regression plots
> 
> Usage:
>  python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> """
> 
> import os, json, argparse, glob, subprocess, csv
> import pandas as pd
> import numpy as np
> import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
> import seaborn as sns
> 
> try:
>  from tqdm import tqdm
> except Exception:
>  def tqdm(x, **kwargs): return x
> 
> # ------------------------------- Utils -------------------------------- #
> 
> def run_and_capture_json(cmd: str, json_path: str):
>  """Run cmd, capture stdout, validate as JSON, write to json_path."""
>  print(f"[RUN] {cmd}")
>  res = subprocess.run(cmd, shell=True,
>  stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
>  stderr=subprocess.PIPE,
>  text=True)
>  if res.returncode != 0:
>  print(res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Command failed (exit {res.returncode})")
> 
>  out = (res.stdout or "").strip()
>  if not out:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError("No JSON was emitted on stdout by run_qa_analysis.py")
> 
>  try:
>  parsed = json.loads(out)
>  except json.JSONDecodeError as e:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Invalid JSON on stdout: {e}") from e
> 
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(json_path), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(json_path, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(parsed, f, indent=2)
>  return parsed
> 
> def load_json(path: str):
>  with open(path) as f:
>  return json.load(f)
> 
> def sniff_bh_loop_csv(path: str) -> bool:
>  """
>  Return True if file looks like a BH loop (t,H,B).
>  Heuristics:
>  1) Header contains all of {'t','H','B'} (case-insensitive), or
>  2) First non-header numeric row has exactly 3 numeric columns.
>  """
>  try:
>  with open(path, newline='') as fh:
>  first = fh.readline()
>  # header case
>  if any(c.isalpha() for c in first):
>  hdr = [h.strip().lower() for h in first.replace('#','').split(',')]
>  if {'t','h','b'}.issubset(set(hdr)):
>  return True
>  # not a BH header -> likely a log/metadata file
>  return False
> 
>  # numeric-first-line case: count columns
>  cols = [c.strip() for c in first.split(',') if c.strip() != ""]
>  if len(cols) != 3:
>  return False
>  # try casting to float
>  _ = [float(c) for c in cols]
>  return True
>  except Exception:
>  return False
> 
> def normalize_basename_series(s: pd.Series) -> pd.Series:
>  """Map any strings to their basename (strip path) for reliable join keys."""
>  def base(x):
>  try:
>  return os.path.basename(str(x))
>  except Exception:
>  return x
>  return s.apply(base)
> 
> # ----------------------------- Visualization --------------------------- #
> 
> def visualize_correlations(df: pd.DataFrame, outdir: str):
>  """Heatmap + quick regressions for W_h, Phi_QA, mismatch (if present)."""
>  if "W_h" in df.columns and "Phi_QA" in df.columns and "mismatch" not in df.columns:
>  df["mismatch"] = df["W_h"] - df["Phi_QA"]
> 
>  numeric = df.select_dtypes(include=[np.number]).copy()
>  if numeric.empty:
>  print("[INFO] No numeric columns to visualize.")
>  return
> 
>  corr = numeric.corr()
>  plt.figure(figsize=(10, 8))
>  sns.heatmap(corr, cmap="coolwarm", center=0, annot=True)
>  plt.title("QA–Kairospace Correlation Matrix")
>  plt.tight_layout()
>  os.makedirs(outdir, exist_ok=True)
>  plt.savefig(os.path.join(outdir, "qa_kairospace_heatmap.png"))
>  plt.close()
>  print("[OK] Saved heatmap →", os.path.join(outdir, "qa_kairospace_heatmap.png"))
> 
>  # Simple regression set
>  targets = [c for c in ["W_h", "Phi_QA", "mismatch"] if c in numeric.columns]
>  for y in targets:
>  for x in numeric.columns:
>  if x == y:
>  continue
>  try:
>  r = np.corrcoef(df[y], df[x])[0, 1] if len(df) > 1 else np.nan
>  except Exception:
>  r = np.nan
>  plt.figure()
>  sns.regplot(data=df, x=x, y=y, scatter_kws={'s': 50})
>  plt.title(f"{y} vs {x} (r = {r:.2f})")
>  plt.tight_layout()
>  outpath = os.path.join(outdir, f"qa_kairospace_reg_{y}_vs_{x}.png")
>  plt.savefig(outpath)
>  plt.close()
> 
> # ----------------------------- Batch Engine ---------------------------- #
> 
> def evaluate_batch(args):
>  os.makedirs(args.outdir, exist_ok=True)
>  json_root = os.path.join(args.outdir, "json")
>  os.makedirs(json_root, exist_ok=True)
> 
>  # --- Step 1: Calibrate α/β on reference loop ---
>  ref_name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(args.calibrate_on))[0]
>  ref_dir = os.path.join(json_root, ref_name)
>  ref_json = os.path.join(ref_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  if not os.path.exists(ref_json) or os.path.getsize(ref_json) == 0:
>  calib_cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {args.calibrate_on} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {ref_dir}"
>  )
>  calib = run_and_capture_json(calib_cmd, ref_json)
>  else:
>  calib = load_json(ref_json)
> 
>  alpha_X, alpha_J, alpha_K = calib["alpha_X"], calib["alpha_J"], calib["alpha_K"]
>  beta_H, beta_B = calib["beta_H"], calib["beta_B"]
>  print(f"[OK] Loaded calibration α=({alpha_X:.3g},{alpha_J:.3g},{alpha_K:.3g}) "
>  f"β=({beta_H:.3g},{beta_B:.3g})")
> 
>  # --- Step 2: Detect BH loop CSVs and evaluate with fixed α/β ---
>  all_csv = sorted(glob.glob(os.path.join(args.dir, "*.csv")))
>  bh_csv = [p for p in all_csv if sniff_bh_loop_csv(p)]
>  skipped = sorted(set(all_csv) - set(bh_csv))
>  if skipped:
>  print("[INFO] Skipping non-BH CSVs:")
>  for s in skipped:
>  print(" -", s)
> 
>  if not bh_csv:
>  print(f"[WARN] No BH loop CSVs detected under: {args.dir}")
>  records = []
> 
>  for fpath in tqdm(bh_csv, desc="Evaluating loops"):
>  name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(fpath))[0]
>  loop_dir = os.path.join(json_root, name)
>  out_json = os.path.join(loop_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {fpath} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--alphas {alpha_X} {alpha_J} {alpha_K} "
>  f"--betas {beta_H} {beta_B} "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {loop_dir}"
>  )
>  try:
>  rec = run_and_capture_json(cmd, out_json)
>  rec["file"] = os.path.basename(fpath)
>  records.append(rec)
>  except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed on {fpath}: {e}")
> 
>  df = pd.DataFrame(records)
>  if "W_h" in df.columns and "Phi_QA" in df.columns and "mismatch" not in df.columns:
>  df["mismatch"] = df["W_h"] - df["Phi_QA"]
> 
>  summary_csv_path = os.path.join(args.outdir, "summary.csv")
>  df.to_csv(summary_csv_path, index=False)
>  print(f"[OK] Saved {len(df)} rows → {summary_csv_path}")
> 
>  # --- Step 3: Optional merge with experimental log + visualize ---
>  merged_to_plot = df
>  if args.log and os.path.exists(args.log):
>  try:
>  log_df = pd.read_csv(args.log)
> 
>  # pick join key: prefer 'file', else 'filename', else 'label'
>  join_key = None
>  for c in ["file", "filename", "label"]:
>  if c in log_df.columns:
>  join_key = c
>  break
> 
>  if join_key is None:
>  raise KeyError("No join key: expected one of ['file','filename','label'] in log CSV")
> 
>  # normalize to basename and align to df['file']
>  log_df["file"] = normalize_basename_series(log_df[join_key])
>  if "file" not in df.columns:
>  raise KeyError("Internal error: df has no 'file' column after batch run")
> 
>  merged = pd.merge(df, log_df.drop(columns=[join_key], errors='ignore'),
>  on="file", how="left")
>  merged_path = os.path.join(args.outdir, "summary_with_kairospace.csv")
>  merged.to_csv(merged_path, index=False)
>  print(f"[OK] Merged with experimental log → {merged_path}")
>  merged_to_plot = merged
>  except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed merging with log ({args.log}): {e}")
> 
>  visualize_correlations(merged_to_plot, args.outdir)
> 
> # --------------------------------- CLI -------------------------------- #
> 
> def main():
>  ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
>  ap.add_argument("--dir", required=True, help="Directory containing .csv BH loops")
>  ap.add_argument("--seed", nargs=4, required=True, type=float,
>  help="QA seed tuple: b e d a")
>  ap.add_argument("--calibrate-on", required=True,
>  help="CSV file (path) used to globally fit α/β")
>  ap.add_argument("--log", help="Optional experimental log CSV "
>  "(will auto-detect join key: file/filename/label)")
>  ap.add_argument("--outdir", default="qa_batch_results", help="Output directory")
>  args = ap.parse_args()
>  evaluate_batch(args)
> 
> if __name__ == "__main__":
>  main()
> ```
> 
> ### What changed & why
> - **BH loop sniffer**: `sniff_bh_loop_csv()` prevents trying to parse your experiment log as a loop (that “label” error you saw).
> - **Flexible log join**: looks for `file`, else `filename`, else `label`; normalizes to basenames so `mydir/loops/sample_bh_loop.csv` matches `sample_bh_loop.csv`.
> - **Same robust stdout→JSON** capture (no more empty `summary.json`).
> 
> ### Re-run
> ```bash
> python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> ```
> 
> You should see it **skip** the non-BH CSV, write a **3-row summary**, and attempt the merge with the detected key. If your log uses a different key name, tell me what it is and I’ll lock it in.

> Here’s exactly what your two uploaded files contain, and the precise join that works:

> - **`qa_with_kairospace_seed.csv`** 
>  • shape: (9, 28) 
>  • has a **`file`** column (filenames like `N87_BH_loop.csv`, etc.)
> 
> - **`kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv`** 
>  • shape: (5, 12) 
>  • has **`label`** (your loop identifiers), plus metrics like `bubble_count_per_mL`, `DO_mgL`, `CFU_count`, `pH`, `EC`, …
> 
> The fix is to join **`qa.file` ↔ `log.label`** (after normalizing to basenames). I’ve already built that merged table for you and saved it here:
> 
> **[Download merged CSV](https://chat.openai.com/c/68e7f23f-60f4-8333-9005-de691a10b35d) *(visit original conversation to download)***
> 
> It was created by mapping:
> 
> - `qa['file_basename'] = basename(qa['file'])` 
> - `log['file_basename'] = basename(log['label'])` 
> - `merged = qa.merge(log.drop(columns=['label']), on='file_basename', how='left')`
> 
> If you want your **`qa_batch_runner.py`** to do this automatically, change the log-merge block to:
> 
> ```python
> # auto-detect join key and normalize to basename
> join_key = None
> for c in ["file", "filename", "label"]:
>  if c in log_df.columns:
>  join_key = c
>  break
> if join_key is None:
>  raise KeyError("No join key: expected one of ['file','filename','label'] in log CSV")

>  df.drop(columns=["file"], errors="ignore"),

>[!nexus_agent] **Assistant** - 10/10/2025 at 9:41 PM
> Here’s the **full, hardened `qa_batch_runner.py`** with:
> 
> - Robust stdout→JSON capture (no empty files / races)
> - BH-loop sniffer (only runs on real `t,H,B` CSVs)
> - Flexible log join (`file`/`filename`/`label`) **via basename normalization**
> - Writes `summary.csv` and (if `--log`) `summary_with_kairospace.csv`
> - Generates correlation heatmap + quick regressions
> 
> Save this over your current file.
> 
> ```python
> #!/usr/bin/env python3
> """
> QA Batch Runner — Global Calibration Mode (robust, with BH-loop sniffer & flexible log join)
> -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
> - Calibrates α/β on a reference BH loop once
> - Applies fixed α/β to every detected B–H CSV in --dir
> - Captures JSON from run_qa_analysis.py stdout, validates, and writes summary.json
> - Produces summary.csv (+ merged summary_with_kairospace.csv if --log)
> - Emits correlation heatmap and basic regression plots
> 
> Usage:
>  python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> """
> 
> import os, json, argparse, glob, subprocess
> import pandas as pd
> import numpy as np
> import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
> import seaborn as sns
> 
> # tqdm is optional
> try:
>  from tqdm import tqdm
> except Exception:
>  def tqdm(x, **kwargs): return x
> 
> # ------------------------------- Utils -------------------------------- #
> 
> def run_and_capture_json(cmd: str, json_path: str):
>  """Run cmd, capture stdout, validate as JSON, write to json_path."""
>  print(f"[RUN] {cmd}")
>  res = subprocess.run(cmd, shell=True,
>  stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
>  stderr=subprocess.PIPE,
>  text=True)
>  if res.returncode != 0:
>  print(res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Command failed (exit {res.returncode})")
> 
>  out = (res.stdout or "").strip()
>  if not out:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError("No JSON was emitted on stdout by run_qa_analysis.py")
> 
>  try:
>  parsed = json.loads(out)
>  except json.JSONDecodeError as e:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Invalid JSON on stdout: {e}") from e
> 
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(json_path), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(json_path, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(parsed, f, indent=2)
>  return parsed
> 
> def load_json(path: str):
>  with open(path) as f:
>  return json.load(f)
> 
> def sniff_bh_loop_csv(path: str) -> bool:
>  """
>  Return True if file looks like a BH loop (t,H,B).
>  Heuristics:
>  1) Header contains all of {'t','H','B'} (case-insensitive), or
>  2) First non-header numeric row has exactly 3 numeric columns.
>  """
>  try:
>  with open(path, newline='') as fh:
>  first = fh.readline()
>  # header case
>  if any(c.isalpha() for c in first):
>  hdr = [h.strip().lower() for h in first.replace('#','').split(',')]
>  return {'t','h','b'}.issubset(set(hdr))
>  # numeric-first-line case: require 3 numeric columns
>  cols = [c.strip() for c in first.split(',') if c.strip() != ""]
>  if len(cols) != 3:
>  return False
>  _ = [float(c) for c in cols] # will raise if not numeric
>  return True
>  except Exception:
>  return False
> 
> def basename_series(s: pd.Series) -> pd.Series:
>  """Map strings to their basename (strip directories)."""
>  def base(x):
>  try:
>  return os.path.basename(str(x))
>  except Exception:
>  return x
>  return s.apply(base)
> 
> # ----------------------------- Visualization --------------------------- #
> 
> def visualize_correlations(df: pd.DataFrame, outdir: str):
>  """Heatmap + quick regressions for W_h, Phi_QA, mismatch (if present)."""
>  if "W_h" in df.columns and "Phi_QA" in df.columns and "mismatch" not in df.columns:
>  df["mismatch"] = df["W_h"] - df["Phi_QA"]
> 
>  numeric = df.select_dtypes(include=[np.number]).copy()
>  if numeric.empty:
>  print("[INFO] No numeric columns to visualize.")
>  return
> 
>  corr = numeric.corr()
>  plt.figure(figsize=(10, 8))
>  sns.heatmap(corr, cmap="coolwarm", center=0, annot=True)
>  plt.title("QA–Kairospace Correlation Matrix")
>  plt.tight_layout()
>  os.makedirs(outdir, exist_ok=True)
>  heatmap_path = os.path.join(outdir, "qa_kairospace_heatmap.png")
>  plt.savefig(heatmap_path)
>  plt.close()
>  print("[OK] Saved heatmap →", heatmap_path)
> 
>  # Simple regression set
>  targets = [c for c in ["W_h", "Phi_QA", "mismatch"] if c in numeric.columns]
>  for y in targets:
>  for x in numeric.columns:
>  if x == y:
>  continue
>  try:
>  r = np.corrcoef(df[y], df[x])[0, 1] if len(df) > 1 else np.nan
>  except Exception:
>  r = np.nan
>  plt.figure()
>  sns.regplot(data=df, x=x, y=y, scatter_kws={'s': 50})
>  plt.title(f"{y} vs {x} (r = {r:.2f})")
>  plt.tight_layout()
>  outpath = os.path.join(outdir, f"qa_kairospace_reg_{y}_vs_{x}.png")
>  plt.savefig(outpath)
>  plt.close()
> 
> # ----------------------------- Batch Engine ---------------------------- #
> 
> def evaluate_batch(args):
>  os.makedirs(args.outdir, exist_ok=True)
>  json_root = os.path.join(args.outdir, "json")
>  os.makedirs(json_root, exist_ok=True)
> 
>  # --- Step 1: Calibrate α/β on reference loop ---
>  ref_name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(args.calibrate_on))[0]
>  ref_dir = os.path.join(json_root, ref_name)
>  ref_json = os.path.join(ref_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  if not os.path.exists(ref_json) or os.path.getsize(ref_json) == 0:
>  calib_cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {args.calibrate_on} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {ref_dir}"
>  )
>  calib = run_and_capture_json(calib_cmd, ref_json)
>  else:
>  calib = load_json(ref_json)
> 
>  alpha_X, alpha_J, alpha_K = calib["alpha_X"], calib["alpha_J"], calib["alpha_K"]
>  beta_H, beta_B = calib["beta_H"], calib["beta_B"]
>  print(f"[OK] Loaded calibration α=({alpha_X:.3g},{alpha_J:.3g},{alpha_K:.3g}) "
>  f"β=({beta_H:.3g},{beta_B:.3g})")
> 
>  # --- Step 2: Detect BH loop CSVs and evaluate with fixed α/β ---
>  all_csv = sorted(glob.glob(os.path.join(args.dir, "*.csv")))
>  bh_csv = [p for p in all_csv if sniff_bh_loop_csv(p)]
>  skipped = sorted(set(all_csv) - set(bh_csv))
>  if skipped:
>  print("[INFO] Skipping non-BH CSVs:")
>  for s in skipped:
>  print(" -", s)
> 
>  if not bh_csv:
>  print(f"[WARN] No BH loop CSVs detected under: {args.dir}")
>  records = []
> 
>  for fpath in tqdm(bh_csv, desc="Evaluating loops"):
>  name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(fpath))[0]
>  loop_dir = os.path.join(json_root, name)
>  out_json = os.path.join(loop_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {fpath} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--alphas {alpha_X} {alpha_J} {alpha_K} "
>  f"--betas {beta_H} {beta_B} "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {loop_dir}"
>  )
>  try:
>  rec = run_and_capture_json(cmd, out_json)
>  rec["file"] = os.path.basename(fpath)
>  records.append(rec)
>  except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed on {fpath}: {e}")
> 
>  df = pd.DataFrame(records)
>  if "W_h" in df.columns and "Phi_QA" in df.columns and "mismatch" not in df.columns:
>  df["mismatch"] = df["W_h"] - df["Phi_QA"]
> 
>  summary_csv_path = os.path.join(args.outdir, "summary.csv")
>  df.to_csv(summary_csv_path, index=False)
>  print(f"[OK] Saved {len(df)} rows → {summary_csv_path}")
> 
>  # --- Step 3: Optional merge with experimental log + visualize ---
>  merged_to_plot = df
>  if args.log and os.path.exists(args.log):
>  try:
>  log_df = pd.read_csv(args.log)
> 
>  # pick join key: prefer 'file', else 'filename', else 'label'
>  join_key = None
>  for c in ["file", "filename", "label"]:
>  if c in log_df.columns:
>  join_key = c
>  break
>  if join_key is None:
>  raise KeyError("No join key: expected one of ['file','filename','label'] in log CSV")
> 
>  # normalize to basename and join
>  df_join = df.copy()
>  df_join["file_basename"] = basename_series(df_join["file"]) if "file" in df_join.columns else None
> 
>  log_df = log_df.copy()
>  log_df["file_basename"] = basename_series(log_df[join_key])
> 
>  # show unmatched rows for quick debugging
>  left_keys = set(df_join["file_basename"].dropna()) if "file_basename" in df_join.columns else set()
>  right_keys = set(log_df["file_basename"].dropna())
>  missing_in_log = sorted(left_keys - right_keys)
>  missing_in_df = sorted(right_keys - left_keys)
>  if missing_in_log:
>  print("[INFO] In QA output but missing in log:", missing_in_log)
>  if missing_in_df:
>  print("[INFO] In log but missing in QA output:", missing_in_df)
> 
>  merged = pd.merge(
>  df_join.drop(columns=["file"], errors="ignore"),
>  log_df.drop(columns=[join_key], errors="ignore"),
>  on="file_basename", how="left"
>  )
>  merged_path = os.path.join(args.outdir, "summary_with_kairospace.csv")
>  merged.to_csv(merged_path, index=False)
>  print(f"[OK] Merged with experimental log → {merged_path}")
>  merged_to_plot = merged
>  except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed merging with log ({args.log}): {e}")
> 
>  visualize_correlations(merged_to_plot, args.outdir)
> 
> # --------------------------------- CLI -------------------------------- #
> 
> def main():
>  ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
>  ap.add_argument("--dir", required=True, help="Directory containing .csv BH loops")
>  ap.add_argument("--seed", nargs=4, required=True, type=float,
>  help="QA seed tuple: b e d a")
>  ap.add_argument("--calibrate-on", required=True,
>  help="CSV file (path) used to globally fit α/β")
>  ap.add_argument("--log", help="Optional experimental log CSV "
>  "(auto-detect join key: file/filename/label)")
>  ap.add_argument("--outdir", default="qa_batch_results", help="Output directory")
>  args = ap.parse_args()
>  evaluate_batch(args)
> 
> if __name__ == "__main__":
>  main()
> ```
> 
> Run it:
> 
> ```bash
> python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> ```
> 
> If anything barks, paste the first ~30 lines of the console output and I’ll zero in fast.

>[!nexus_agent] **Assistant** - 10/10/2025 at 9:51 PM
> Great run. You’re merged and plotting — the only remaining issue is exactly what the logs say:
> 
> - Your **QA output uses filenames** (`N87_BH_loop.csv`, `N87_BH_loop_noheader.csv`)
> - Your **experiment log uses experiment labels** (`CFU_Control_8ppm`, `Product_UpTo_500M_DOx4`, …)
> 
> Those don’t match, so the join is empty (NaNs → heatmap warnings).
> 
> Below is a **drop-in full script** that keeps all your working behavior AND adds two small quality-of-life features so you can finish the merge cleanly:
> 
> 1) `--label-to-file-csv` — optional tiny mapping file with two columns:
>  ```
>  label,file
>  CFU_Control_8ppm,N87_BH_loop.csv
>  CFU_MedDO_12ppm,N87_BH_loop_noheader.csv
>  ```
>  The runner will apply this mapping to your log before merging.
> 
> 2) `--include-pattern` — optional `glob` (e.g. `*sample*`) if you want to **force-include** a file the sniffer skipped (e.g. `sample_bh_loop.csv`).
> 
> Everything else (stdout→JSON capture, BH sniffer, plots) stays the same.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## `qa_batch_runner.py` (updated)
> 
> ```python
> #!/usr/bin/env python3
> """
> QA Batch Runner — Global Calibration Mode (robust, sniffer, flexible log join + mapping)
> ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
> - Calibrates α/β on a reference BH loop once
> - Applies fixed α/β to every detected B–H CSV in --dir
> - Captures JSON from run_qa_analysis.py stdout, validates, writes summary.json
> - Produces summary.csv (+ merged summary_with_kairospace.csv if --log)
> - Emits correlation heatmap + quick regressions
> - NEW: --label-to-file-csv to map experiment log labels → BH filenames
> - NEW: --include-pattern to force-include specific files (override sniffer)
> 
> Usage:
>  python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --label-to-file-csv label_to_file_map.csv \
>  --include-pattern "*sample*" \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> """
> 
> import os, json, argparse, glob, subprocess
> import pandas as pd
> import numpy as np
> import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
> import seaborn as sns
> 
> # tqdm is optional
> try:
>  from tqdm import tqdm
> except Exception:
>  def tqdm(x, **kwargs): return x
> 
> # ------------------------------- Utils -------------------------------- #
> 
> def run_and_capture_json(cmd: str, json_path: str):
>  """Run cmd, capture stdout, validate as JSON, write to json_path."""
>  print(f"[RUN] {cmd}")
>  res = subprocess.run(cmd, shell=True,
>  stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
>  stderr=subprocess.PIPE,
>  text=True)
>  if res.returncode != 0:
>  print(res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Command failed (exit {res.returncode})")
> 
>  out = (res.stdout or "").strip()
>  if not out:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError("No JSON was emitted on stdout by run_qa_analysis.py")
> 
>  try:
>  parsed = json.loads(out)
>  except json.JSONDecodeError as e:
>  print("STDERR from child:\n", res.stderr)
>  raise RuntimeError(f"Invalid JSON on stdout: {e}") from e
> 
>  os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(json_path), exist_ok=True)
>  with open(json_path, "w") as f:
>  json.dump(parsed, f, indent=2)
>  return parsed
> 
> def load_json(path: str):
>  with open(path) as f:
>  return json.load(f)
> 
> def sniff_bh_loop_csv(path: str) -> bool:
>  """
>  Return True if file looks like a BH loop (t,H,B).
>  Heuristics:
>  1) Header contains all of {'t','H','B'} (case-insensitive), or
>  2) First non-header numeric row has exactly 3 numeric columns.
>  """
>  try:
>  with open(path, newline='') as fh:
>  first = fh.readline()
>  # header case
>  if any(c.isalpha() for c in first):
>  hdr = [h.strip().lower() for h in first.replace('#','').split(',')]
>  return {'t','h','b'}.issubset(set(hdr))
>  # numeric-first-line case: require 3 numeric columns
>  cols = [c.strip() for c in first.split(',') if c.strip() != ""]
>  if len(cols) != 3:
>  return False
>  _ = [float(c) for c in cols] # will raise if not numeric
>  return True
>  except Exception:
>  return False
> 
> def basename_series(s: pd.Series) -> pd.Series:
>  """Map strings to their basename (strip directories)."""
>  def base(x):
>  try:
>  return os.path.basename(str(x))
>  except Exception:
>  return x
>  return s.apply(base)
> 
> def load_label_map(path: str) -> dict:
>  """
>  Load a CSV mapping: label,file
>  Returns dict mapping label -> file_basename
>  """
>  df = pd.read_csv(path)
>  if not {'label','file'}.issubset(df.columns):
>  raise ValueError("label-to-file CSV must have columns: label,file")
>  out = {}
>  for _, row in df.iterrows():
>  lab = str(row['label'])
>  fil = os.path.basename(str(row['file']))
>  out[lab] = fil
>  return out
> 
> # ----------------------------- Visualization --------------------------- #
> 
> def visualize_correlations(df: pd.DataFrame, outdir: str):
>  """Heatmap + quick regressions for W_h, Phi_QA, mismatch (if present)."""
>  if "W_h" in df.columns and "Phi_QA" in df.columns and "mismatch" not in df.columns:
>  df["mismatch"] = df["W_h"] - df["Phi_QA"]
> 
>  numeric = df.select_dtypes(include=[np.number]).copy()
>  if numeric.empty:
>  print("[INFO] No numeric columns to visualize.")
>  return
> 
>  corr = numeric.corr()
>  plt.figure(figsize=(10, 8))
>  sns.heatmap(corr, cmap="coolwarm", center=0, annot=True)
>  plt.title("QA–Kairospace Correlation Matrix")
>  plt.tight_layout()
>  os.makedirs(outdir, exist_ok=True)
>  heatmap_path = os.path.join(outdir, "qa_kairospace_heatmap.png")
>  plt.savefig(heatmap_path)
>  plt.close()
>  print("[OK] Saved heatmap →", heatmap_path)
> 
>  # Simple regression set
>  targets = [c for c in ["W_h", "Phi_QA", "mismatch"] if c in numeric.columns]
>  for y in targets:
>  for x in numeric.columns:
>  if x == y:
>  continue
>  try:
>  r = np.corrcoef(df[y], df[x])[0, 1] if len(df) > 1 else np.nan
>  except Exception:
>  r = np.nan
>  plt.figure()
>  sns.regplot(data=df, x=x, y=y, scatter_kws={'s': 50})
>  plt.title(f"{y} vs {x} (r = {r:.2f})")
>  plt.tight_layout()
>  outpath = os.path.join(outdir, f"qa_kairospace_reg_{y}_vs_{x}.png")
>  plt.savefig(outpath)
>  plt.close()
> 
> # ----------------------------- Batch Engine ---------------------------- #
> 
> def evaluate_batch(args):
>  os.makedirs(args.outdir, exist_ok=True)
>  json_root = os.path.join(args.outdir, "json")
>  os.makedirs(json_root, exist_ok=True)
> 
>  # --- Step 1: Calibrate α/β on reference loop ---
>  ref_name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(args.calibrate_on))[0]
>  ref_dir = os.path.join(json_root, ref_name)
>  ref_json = os.path.join(ref_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  if not os.path.exists(ref_json) or os.path.getsize(ref_json) == 0:
>  calib_cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {args.calibrate_on} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--calibrate-alphas --calibrate-betas "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {ref_dir}"
>  )
>  calib = run_and_capture_json(calib_cmd, ref_json)
>  else:
>  calib = load_json(ref_json)
> 
>  alpha_X, alpha_J, alpha_K = calib["alpha_X"], calib["alpha_J"], calib["alpha_K"]
>  beta_H, beta_B = calib["beta_H"], calib["beta_B"]
>  print(f"[OK] Loaded calibration α=({alpha_X:.3g},{alpha_J:.3g},{alpha_K:.3g}) "
>  f"β=({beta_H:.3g},{beta_B:.3g})")
> 
>  # --- Step 2: Detect BH loop CSVs (optionally include pattern) and evaluate ---
>  all_csv = sorted(glob.glob(os.path.join(args.dir, "*.csv")))
>  bh_csv = [p for p in all_csv if sniff_bh_loop_csv(p)]
> 
>  # Force-include pattern if provided
>  if args.include_pattern:
>  forced = sorted(glob.glob(os.path.join(args.dir, args.include_pattern)))
>  for p in forced:
>  if p not in bh_csv and p in all_csv:
>  bh_csv.append(p)
>  bh_csv = sorted(set(bh_csv))
> 
>  skipped = sorted(set(all_csv) - set(bh_csv))
>  if skipped:
>  print("[INFO] Skipping non-BH CSVs:")
>  for s in skipped:
>  print(" -", s)
> 
>  if not bh_csv:
>  print(f"[WARN] No BH loop CSVs detected under: {args.dir}")
>  records = []
> 
>  for fpath in tqdm(bh_csv, desc="Evaluating loops"):
>  name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(fpath))[0]
>  loop_dir = os.path.join(json_root, name)
>  out_json = os.path.join(loop_dir, "summary.json")
> 
>  cmd = (
>  f"python run_qa_analysis.py --file {fpath} "
>  f"--seed {args.seed[0]} {args.seed[1]} {args.seed[2]} {args.seed[3]} "
>  f"--alphas {alpha_X} {alpha_J} {alpha_K} "
>  f"--betas {beta_H} {beta_B} "
>  f"--save-plots --outdir {loop_dir}"
>  )
>  try:
>  rec = run_and_capture_json(cmd, out_json)
>  rec["file"] = os.path.basename(fpath)
>  records.append(rec)
>  except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed on {fpath}: {e}")
> 
>  df = pd.DataFrame(records)
>  if "W_h" in df.columns and "Phi_QA" in df.columns and "mismatch" not in df.columns:
>  df["mismatch"] = df["W_h"] - df["Phi_QA"]
> 
>  summary_csv_path = os.path.join(args.outdir, "summary.csv")
>  df.to_csv(summary_csv_path, index=False)
>  print(f"[OK] Saved {len(df)} rows → {summary_csv_path}")
> 
>  # --- Step 3: Optional merge with experimental log + visualize ---
>  merged_to_plot = df
>  if args.log and os.path.exists(args.log):
>  try:
>  log_df = pd.read_csv(args.log)
> 
>  # apply optional label->file mapping
>  if args.label_to_file_csv:
>  mapping = load_label_map(args.label_to_file_csv)
>  # create a normalized 'file' column from label
>  if "label" not in log_df.columns:
>  raise KeyError("Mapping requires 'label' in the log CSV.")
>  log_df["file"] = log_df["label"].map(mapping).astype(object)
> 
>  # pick join key: prefer 'file', else 'filename', else 'label'
>  join_key = None
>  for c in ["file", "filename", "label"]:
>  if c in log_df.columns:
>  join_key = c
>  break
>  if join_key is None:
>  raise KeyError("No join key: expected one of ['file','filename','label'] in log CSV")
> 
>  # normalize to basename on both sides
>  df_join = df.copy()
>  df_join["file_basename"] = basename_series(df_join["file"]) if "file" in df_join.columns else None
>  log_df = log_df.copy()
>  log_df["file_basename"] = basename_series(log_df[join_key])
> 
>  # show unmatched rows
>  left_keys = set(df_join["file_basename"].dropna()) if "file_basename" in df_join.columns else set()
>  right_keys = set(log_df["file_basename"].dropna())
>  missing_in_log = sorted(left_keys - right_keys)
>  missing_in_df = sorted(right_keys - left_keys)
>  if missing_in_log:
>  print("[INFO] In QA output but missing in log:", missing_in_log)
>  if missing_in_df:
>  print("[INFO] In log but missing in QA output:", missing_in_df)
> 
>  merged = pd.merge(
>  df_join.drop(columns=["file"], errors="ignore"),
>  log_df.drop(columns=[join_key], errors="ignore"),
>  on="file_basename", how="left"
>  )
>  merged_path = os.path.join(args.outdir, "summary_with_kairospace.csv")
>  merged.to_csv(merged_path, index=False)
>  print(f"[OK] Merged with experimental log → {merged_path}")
>  merged_to_plot = merged
>  except Exception as e:
>  print(f"[WARN] Failed merging with log ({args.log}): {e}")
> 
>  visualize_correlations(merged_to_plot, args.outdir)
> 
> # --------------------------------- CLI -------------------------------- #
> 
> def main():
>  ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
>  ap.add_argument("--dir", required=True, help="Directory containing .csv BH loops")
>  ap.add_argument("--seed", nargs=4, required=True, type=float,
>  help="QA seed tuple: b e d a")
>  ap.add_argument("--calibrate-on", required=True,
>  help="CSV file (path) used to globally fit α/β")
>  ap.add_argument("--log", help="Optional experimental log CSV (auto-detect join key: file/filename/label)")
>  ap.add_argument("--label-to-file-csv", help="Optional CSV mapping: label,file (to map log labels → BH filenames)")
>  ap.add_argument("--include-pattern", help="Optional glob to force-include BH files (e.g. '*sample*')")
>  ap.add_argument("--outdir", default="qa_batch_results", help="Output directory")
>  args = ap.parse_args()
>  evaluate_batch(args)
> 
> if __name__ == "__main__":
>  main()
> ```
> 
> ---
> 
> ## How to use the mapping (so the merge actually fills)
> 
> Create `label_to_file_map.csv` like this (adjust to your truth):
> 
> ```csv
> label,file
> CFU_Control_8ppm,N87_BH_loop.csv
> CFU_MedDO_12ppm,N87_BH_loop_noheader.csv
> CFU_HighDO_24ppm,N87_BH_loop_noheader.csv
> Kairo_NTA_600M,N87_BH_loop.csv
> Product_UpTo_500M_DOx4,N87_BH_loop.csv
> ```
> 
> Then run:
> 
> ```bash
> python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --label-to-file-csv label_to_file_map.csv \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> ```
> 
> If you want to force-include `sample_bh_loop.csv`:
> 
> ```bash
> python qa_batch_runner.py \
>  --dir loops/ \
>  --seed 1 1 2 3 \
>  --calibrate-on loops/N87_BH_loop.csv \
>  --log kairospace_seed_experiment_log.csv \
>  --label-to-file-csv label_to_file_map.csv \
>  --include-pattern "sample_bh_loop.csv" \
>  --outdir qa_batch_results/
> ```
> 
> This gets you a **non-NaN merged table** and stable plots, without guessing any semantics on my end.
